Default parameters were used for StringTie with the --merge flag to produce a set of non-redundant transcripts to feed into MAKER. These transcripts were treated as expressed sequence tag evidence and protein sequences from Arabidopsis<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 17" title="Initiative, A. G. Analysis of the genome sequence of the flowering plant Arabidopsis thaliana. Nature &#xA;                           408, 796 (2000)." href="/articles/s41467-017-02546-5#ref-CR17" id="ref-link-section-d29428e1527">17</a></sup>, <i>Selaginella moellendorffii</i>
                           <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Banks, J. A. et al. The Selaginella genome identifies genetic changes associated with the evolution of vascular plants. science &#xA;                           332, 960–963 (2011)." href="/articles/s41467-017-02546-5#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d29428e1534">10</a></sup>, and UniprotKB plant databases<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Boutet, E., Lieberherr, D., Tognolli, M., Schneider, M. &amp; Bairoch, A. UniProtKB/Swiss-Prot: the manually annotated section of the UniProt KnowledgeBase. Methods Mol. Biol, 406, 89–112 (2007)." href="/articles/s41467-017-02546-5#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d29428e1538">55</a></sup> were used as protein homology evidence. Intact <i>S. lepidophylla</i> LTR retrotransposons were input as a custom repeat database along with default repeat libraries in MAKER. Ab initio gene prediction was done using the gene predictors SNAP and Augustus with reiterative training in <i>S. lepidophylla</i>. The initial MAKER Max gene set was filtered for gene models with Pfam domain evidence and annotation edit distance &lt;1.0. Putative transposon-derived models were removed. This produced a set of 39,051 filtered gene models. A further 11,847 duplicated gene models corresponding to separate haplotypes were removed to produce a final set of 27,204 non-redundant genes.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec15">Orthogroup annotation</h3><p>Orthogroups were identified using Orthofinder (V1.0.6)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="Emms, D. M. &amp; Kelly, S. OrthoFinder: solving fundamental biases in whole genome comparisons dramatically improves orthogroup inference accuracy. Genome Biol. &#xA;                           16, 157 (2015)." href="/articles/s41467-017-02546-5#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d29428e1556">56</a></sup> with protein-coding genes from the Arabidopsis<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 17" title="Initiative, A. G. Analysis of the genome sequence of the flowering plant Arabidopsis thaliana. Nature &#xA;                           408, 796 (2000)." href="/articles/s41467-017-02546-5#ref-CR17" id="ref-link-section-d29428e1560">17</a></sup>, rice<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 57" title="Goff, S. A. et al. A draft sequence of the rice genome (Oryza sativa L. ssp. japonica). Science &#xA;                           296, 92–100 (2002)." href="/articles/s41467-017-02546-5#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d29428e1564">57</a></sup>, poplar<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Tuskan, G. A. et al. The genome of black cottonwood, Populus trichocarpa (Torr. &amp; Gray). science &#xA;                           313, 1596–1604 (2006)." href="/articles/s41467-017-02546-5#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d29428e1568">58</a></sup>, grape<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Jaillon, O. et al. The grapevine genome sequence suggests ancestral hexaploidization in major angiosperm phyla. Nature &#xA;                           449, 463–467 (2007)." href="/articles/s41467-017-02546-5#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d29428e1572">59</a></sup>, <i>Oropetium thomaeum</i>
                           <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="VanBuren, R. et al. Single-molecule sequencing of the desiccation-tolerant grass Oropetium thomaeum. Nature &#xA;                           527, 508–511 (2015)." href="/articles/s41467-017-02546-5#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d29428e1580">60</a></sup>, <i>S. moellendorffii</i>
                           <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Banks, J. A. et al. The Selaginella genome identifies genetic changes associated with the evolution of vascular plants. science &#xA;                           332, 960–963 (2011)." href="/articles/s41467-017-02546-5#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d29428e1587">10</a></sup>, and <i>S. lepidophylla</i> genomes using default settings (Supplementary Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-017-02546-5#MOESM1">11</a>). We set a stringent cutoff of a 5 fold difference in orthogroup composition and at least a minimum of 10 genes (average) across either Angiosperms or <i>Selaginella</i> groups to identify expanded orthogroups. On average, angiosperm enriched orthogroups had 20-fold enrichment and <i>Selaginella</i> had 40 fold enrichment.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec16">Gene expression analysis</h3><p>Adapter sequences and low-quality bases were filtered from the raw, paired end Illumina RNAseq reads using TRIMMOMATIC (v0.33)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="Bolger, A. M., Lohse, M. &amp; Usadel, B. Trimmomatic: a flexible trimmer for Illumina sequence data. Bioinformatics &#xA;                           30, 2117–2120(2014)." href="/articles/s41467-017-02546-5#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d29428e1612">61</a></sup> and reads shorter than 36 bp were discarded. Expression levels (in Transcript Per Million, TPM) were quantified using Kallisto<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="Bray, N. L., Pimentel, H., Melsted, P. &amp; Pachter, L. Near-optimal probabilistic RNA-seq quantification. Nat. Biotechnol. &#xA;                           34, 525–527 (2016)." href="/articles/s41467-017-02546-5#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d29428e1616">62</a></sup> with the 27,204 monoploid <i>S. lepidophylla</i> gene models provided as input. An average TPM for each time-point was calculated from the mean TPM of the three biological replicates. We preformed weighted gene co-expression analysis of the dehydration and subsequent rehydration time course RNA-seq data with the R package WGCNA<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="Langfelder, P. &amp; Horvath, S. WGCNA: an R package for weighted correlation network analysis. BMC Bioinformatics&#xA;                            9, 1 (2008)." href="/articles/s41467-017-02546-5#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d29428e1623">63</a></sup>. The expression data were pre-filtered to remove genes with excessive missing values or invariant expression using the built-in quality control function. A signed co-expression network was constructed using a soft-thresholding power of 10 and default parameters. The only exception was the mergeCutHeight parameter, controlling the minimum distance between co-expression clusters, which was set to 0.15. The co-expression network resulted in 38 clusters, with 13 genes not placed in any cluster.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec17">MethylC-seq analysis</h3><p>Quality filtered MethylC-seq reads were filtered as described above. Three replicates for 0 h, 24 h, and 120 h post rehydration and unconverted control DNA were sequenced. The average genome coverage of each library is 12.3×. Reads were mapped to the in silico converted, unmasked <i>S. lepidophylla</i> genome for the forward and reverse strands using Bismark (v0.12.0)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="Krueger, F. &amp; Andrews, S. R. Bismark: a flexible aligner and methylation caller for Bisulfite-Seq applications. Bioinformatics &#xA;                           27, 1571–1572 (2011)." href="/articles/s41467-017-02546-5#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d29428e1638">64</a></sup>. Genome-wide cytosine methylation was obtained using the following parameters in the Bismark methylation extractor step: –comprehensive –CX_context --cytosine_report. The methylation level of each CHH, CHG, and CpG position was calculated as the number of methylated count/total of methylated and unmethylated count. Any position with coverage of less than three reads was removed. For each cytosine position, the average methylation level was calculated from the mean methylation level among biological replicates.</p><p>Methylation level of the upstream (1 kb), downstream (1 kb) and body (from transcription start site to transcription stop site) of all genic regions and intact LTR retrotransposons were calculated using BEDTools (v2.24.0)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="Quinlan, A. R. &amp; Hall, I. M. BEDTools: a flexible suite of utilities for comparing genomic features. Bioinformatics &#xA;                           26, 841–842 (2010)." href="/articles/s41467-017-02546-5#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d29428e1645">65</a></sup> and in-house scripts. To study differential methylated regions between 0 h, 24 h, and 120 h post rehydration samples, the whole-genome methylated count of each library was obtained from the Bismark output. Differential methylated regions were analyzed using the R package methylKit (v1.2.0)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="Akalin, A. et al. methylKit: a comprehensive R package for the analysis of genome-wide DNA methylation profiles. Genome Biol. &#xA;                           13, R87 (2012)." href="/articles/s41467-017-02546-5#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d29428e1649">66</a></sup> in 100 bp window and minimum coverage of 10 reads per site.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading c-article__sub-heading--divider" id="Sec18">Data availability</h3><p>The genome assembly, raw PacBio, Illumina DNAseq, and RNAseq data are available from the National Center for Biotechnology Information (NCBI) Short Read Archive (SRA). The RNAseq reads were deposited to NCBI SRA under BioProject PRJNA420971 (BioSample SAMN08128719–08128734) and MethylCseq data were deposited under BioProject PRJNA421023 (BioSample SAMN08132846-08132853). The genome assembly has been deposited under BioSample SAMN07071123 and BioProject ID PRJNA386571.</p></div></div></section>

                </p></li><li class="c-article-references__item js-c-reading-companion-references-item" itemprop="citation" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/ScholarlyArticle"><meta itemprop="author" content="JA. Banks, " /><meta itemprop="datePublished" content="2011" /><meta itemprop="headline" content="Banks, J. A. et al.
